**The *Huangdi Neijing* (Lingshu) – *Jizhu* (Collected Commentaries) – Volume 21: Official Functions – Section 73**

The *Huangdi Neijing* (Lingshu) – *Jizhu* (Collected Commentaries) – Volume 21: **Official Functions** – Section 73

---

Huangdi asked Qibó: *"I have heard of the Nine Needles from my teacher, and their applications are numerous beyond counting. I have reviewed them and condensed them into one system. I recite them, and you discern their principles. If I err, correct me. Please establish the Dao/Way so that it may endure in transmission, and future generations will face no difficulty. Only pass it to the worthy—if not, do not speak of it."*

Qibó bowed twice in respect: *"Please, I shall listen to the Sage-King’s Dao/Way."*

Huangdi said: *"The principles of acupuncture must know the location of form and **qi**—left and right, above and below, the exterior and interior of yin and yang, the abundance or scarcity of blood and **qi**, their direction of flow (whether inverse or顺, *shùn*), and the proper depth of insertion and withdrawal. One must measure the efficacy of treatment to avoid excess. Know how to resolve rigidity, how to supplement deficiency and drain excess, how to regulate the upper and lower **qi** gates, and how to make the channels clear and connect with the Four Seas. Carefully determine their locations: when **qi** struggles between cold and heat, or when exposed to wind and rain, adjust and harmonize accordingly. Understand how to regulate **qi**, grasp the pathways of the channels, know the connections of the left and right limbs#1, and fully comprehend their junctions.

When yin and yang are not in harmony, one knows the time of onset. By examining the beginning and end, discerning the cold and heat, and locating the pathogenic **qi**, even ten thousand needlings will not fail. Thus, one knows the nine functions of the needles, and the Dao/Way of needling is complete.

Understanding the Five Outputs#3, one knows where the **qi** flows swiftly or slowly, and the proper flexion, extension, insertion, and withdrawal all follow clear principles. When yin and yang#3 are combined with the Five Phases, the Five Zàng organs and Six Fǔ viscera also have their own hidden correspondences. The Four Seasons and Eight Winds all contain yin and yang, each occupying its proper place and aligning with the Bright Hall#2. Observing their respective color divisions, one examines where pain arises in the Five Zàng organs and Six Fǔ viscera—left, right, above, or below—and knows whether the **qi** is cold or warm, which channel is affected.

Carefully assessing the cold, warm, smooth, or rough nature of the skin, one knows where the patient suffers. The diaphragm has upper and lower aspects, and one must know where the **qi** resides. First, grasp the Dao/Way, then needle sparsely and loosely, gradually probing while leaving the needle in place, thus achieving a gradual insertion.

If great heat is above, push it downward; if **qi** rises from below, draw it away. For pain in front, always take the point first.

If great cold is outside, retain the needle to supplement; if it enters the interior, follow the method of draining excess.

Where acupuncture fails, moxibustion is appropriate. If the upper **qi** is insufficient, push and elevate it; if the lower **qi** is insufficient, accumulate and follow its flow. When both yin and yang are deficient, fire will naturally correct it.

In cases of severe cold with sudden onset, if the bone channels sink downward or cold descends past the knee to three *lǐ* below, where the yin vessels pass, retain the needle to stop it. If cold enters the interior, push and disperse it. Where channels sink downward, fire will correct them; where rigid vessels are tightly bound, fire will treat them.

If one does not know where the suffering lies, needling below the *liángjiāo*#2 points—whether male yin or female yang—is forbidden to skilled practitioners. Thus concludes the discourse on needling.*

*The proper use of needles must follow established principles: observe celestial light above, align with the Eight Correct#2 below, and thereby avoid strange pathogenic influences. Examine the people’s conditions, distinguishing deficiency from excess, and do not violate their pathogenic **qi**. This way, one attains the Heavenly Dew, meets the year’s emptiness, and rescues without overpowering—otherwise, one risks inviting retribution.

Hence it is said: ‘One must know the Heavenly Prohibitions before speaking of acupuncture intent.’*

*Modeling oneself on the past and verifying with the present, observing the hidden and understanding the boundless, the refined practitioner values what the coarse cannot see—like the hair’s tip exposed. The pathogenic **qi** entering the body, when stirred by alcohol, causes movement in the form. When the proper and pathogenic **qi** enter the body, subtle changes first appear in the complexion. One may not perceive them on the body itself—sometimes present, sometimes absent, sometimes lost, sometimes retained—with or without visible form, and no one knows their true nature.*

*Therefore, the superior practitioner takes **qi** before its sprouting; the inferior practitioner waits until it has fully manifested, then damages the form by treating it.*

Is thus the method of the practitioner’s use of acupuncture: knowing where the **qi** resides, and guarding its pathways, clear in regulating **qi**, filling and emptying as needed, adjusting the speed of insertion and withdrawal, and choosing the proper points for treatment.

Filling must employ a circular motion—cutting and turning, so that the **qi** may flow. Withdrawing swiftly yet exiting slowly, the pathogenic **qi** is expelled; extending to meet it, enlarging the orifice distantly, the **qi** exits swiftly.

Supplementing must employ a square motion—drawing outward the skin, aligning it with the pathway, pulling leftward at the pivot, pushing rightward at the flesh, rotating gently yet pushing steadily, ensuring precision, maintaining correctness, achieving tranquility, steadfastness of heart without wavering, intending subtlety to preserve, then driving the **qi** downward and withdrawing it swiftly. Covering the skin, sealing the outer pathway, the true **qi** is thus retained.

The essentials of acupuncture: never forget its spiritual principle.

Leigong asked the Yellow Emperor: *"The Needle Treatise* says: ‘Only teach those worthy of it; do not instruct those unworthy.’ How does one know if they can be taught?"

The Yellow Emperor replied: "Each finds their own worthy student, entrusting them according to their ability. Thus they can clarify the practice."

Leigong said: "I wish to hear how abilities are matched to roles."

The Yellow Emperor said: "Those with keen vision may be taught to observe complexion; those with acute hearing may be taught to listen for sounds; those with quick speech and agile words may be taught to expound theories; those whose speech is slow yet calm, whose hands are skillful yet whose minds are steady and discerning, may be taught to apply needles and moxa, to regulate blood and **qi**, and to harmonize all disorders—whether inverted or upright, and to discern yin and yang while mastering all directions.

Those with gentle movements, supple sinews, and harmonious minds may be taught to guide **qi** through exercises; those whose words are swift yet whose actions are light, who scorn others yet possess sharp wit, may be taught to cure disease through spittle and incantations; those with painful nails, poisonous hands, and a tendency to harm others through their work, may be taught to press accumulations and suppress stiffness.

Each finds their own match in ability, then the method may be practiced, and their name shall be renowned. If one does not find their worthy student, their skill shall not be perfected, and their teacher shall be without merit."

Thus it is said: *"Only when one finds the right person should the teaching be spoken; if not the right person, do not transmit it."* This is what is meant.

Those whose hands are poisonous may be taught to test by pressing the tortoise—placing the tortoise beneath a vessel and pressing upon it, and in fifty days it shall die. Those whose hands are gentle may restore it to life as before.

---

**Huangdi asked Qibo:**
*"I wish to diagnose without examining the complexion or taking the pulse, relying solely on the *cù* [尺] to speak of the disease, and from the exterior to know the interior. How should this be done?"*

**Qibo replied:**
*"Examine the *cù* for its slackness or tension, its smallness or largeness, its smoothness or roughness, the firmness or fragility of its flesh—thus the form of the disease is determined.*

*If one observes above the eye socket a slight ridge as if newly raised, and the neck pulse moves while the patient coughs, and when pressing the upper limbs and feet, the *guān* [官] pulse does not rise, this is *fēngshuǐ* [風水] with skin distension.*

*If the *cù* skin is smooth and its hollows glisten, this is wind.*
*If the *cù* flesh is weak, this is *jiěchuán* [解傳];*
*If one lies comfortably yet loses flesh, this is cold-heat, and it is untreatable.*

*If the *cù* skin is smooth and greasy with luster, this is wind.*
*If the *cù* skin is rough, this is wind *bì* [痹].*
*If the *cù* skin is coarse like the scales of a dried fish, this is *yānyǐn* [水泱飲] (water stagnation).*
*If the *cù* skin is intensely hot and the pulse is strong and restless, this is *wēn* disease [溫病];*
*If the pulse is strong and smooth, the disease is about to surface.*

*If the *cù* skin is cold and the pulse is small, this is diarrhea and *shǎo qì* [少氣] (weak breath).*
*If the *cù* skin is first hot then cold like a torch, this is cold-heat.*
*If the *cù* skin is first cold, then after prolonged pressure becomes hot, this too is cold-heat.*

*If only the elbow is hot, the heat is above the waist;*
*If only the hand is hot, the heat is below the waist.*
*If only the front of the elbow is hot, the chest is hot;*
*If only the back of the elbow is hot, the shoulders and back are hot.*
*If the middle of the arm is hot, the waist and abdomen are hot;*
*If the back of the elbow and the rough *cù* below it for three or four inches are hot, there are worms in the intestines.*

*If the palm is hot, the abdomen is hot;*
*If the palm is cold, the abdomen is cold.*
*If the white flesh above the fish-like mark has greenish veins, there is cold in the stomach.*

*If the *cù* is hot like a torch and the *rényíng* [人迎] pulse is large, bloodletting is required.*
*If the *cù* is firm and large while the pulse is very small, with *shǎo qì* and increasing joy, death will come swiftly.*

*The eyes turn red—disease is in the heart;*
*White—disease is in the lungs;*
*Blue—disease is in the liver;*
*Yellow—disease is in the spleen;*
*Black—disease is in the kidneys.*

*If the yellow color cannot be named, the disease is in the chest.*
*Diagnosing eye pain: if the red veins descend from above and below, this is *Tàiyáng* disease [太陽病];*
*If they ascend from below, this is *Yángmíng* disease [陽明病];*
*If they move from the exterior inward, this is *Shàoyáng* disease [少陽病].*

*Diagnosing cold-heat: if the red veins move up and down to the pupil, and one vein is seen, death will come in one year;*
*If one and a half veins are seen, death will come in a year and a half;*
*If two veins are seen, death will come in two years;*
*If two and a half veins are seen, death will come in two and a half years;*
*If three veins are seen, death will come in three years.*

*Diagnosing tooth decay and pain: if the *yáng* [陽] pulse arrives with excess, the corresponding side alone will be hot—left for left, right for right, upper for upper, lower for lower.*

*Diagnosing blood vessels: if they are mostly red, there is excess heat;*
*If mostly blue, there is pain;*
*If mostly black, this is chronic *bì* [痹];*
*If red, black, and blue are all present, this is cold-heat.*

*If the body aches and the complexion is faintly yellow, if the teeth are yellow with plaque and the nails have yellow at the base, this is *huángdǎn* [黃疸] (jaundice).*
*If one lies comfortably, the urine is yellow-red, and the pulse is small and rough, this indicates no appetite.*

*If a patient’s *cùnkǒu* [寸口] pulse and *rényíng* [人迎] pulse are equal in size and depth, the disease is difficult to cure.*

*In women, if the *shǎo yīn* [少陰] pulse in the hand is violently moving, this indicates pregnancy.*

*In infants, if the hair on the head all stands upright, death is certain.*

*If the ear’s green veins rise, this indicates *chè téng* [掣痛] (sharp, drawing pain).*

*If the stool is red and flaky (*bàn* [瓣]), with diarrhea, and the pulse is small, the hands and feet will be cold, making recovery difficult;*
*If there is diarrhea, the pulse is small, but the hands and feet are warm, the diarrhea will resolve easily.*

*The changes of the four seasons, the dominance of cold and heat—when yin is excessive, yang must follow; when yang is excessive, yin must follow. Thus, yin governs cold, and yang governs heat. Therefore, extreme cold generates heat, and extreme heat generates cold. Hence, it is said: cold begets heat, and heat begets cold—this is the transformation of yin and yang.*

*Thus it is said:*
*Winter injury from cold leads to springtime pestilential heat;*
*Spring injury from wind leads to summer diarrhea and intestinal disorders;*
*Summer injury from heat leads to autumn *jùe nǜè* [疚疟] (intermittent fever);*
*Autumn injury from dampness leads to winter coughing.*

*This is called the sequence of the four seasons.*

The pronunciation is *jùrán* (as in *jù* + *rán*) and *xǔrán* (also written). *Qǔqiū yǔ* (齲丘禹切) refers to tooth decay (*chǐdù* 齿蠹). *Chèchǐ* (掣尺列切).

*Jùe nǜè* (疚疟), pronounced with *jiù* (上音皆), is a form of intermittent fever marked by emaciation.

---
**Section 75: *Zhēn Jié* (Needling Techniques)**

The Yellow Emperor asked Qìbó:
*"I have heard that needling has five stages—how so?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Indeed, there are five stages. The first is **vibrating dust** (*zhènāi*), the second is **lifting the veil** (*fāméng*), the third is **removing claws** (*qùzhuǎ*), the fourth is **piercing garments** (*chèyī*), and the fifth is **dispelling confusion** (*jiěhuò*)."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Master, when you speak of these five stages, I do not yet grasp their meaning."*

Qìbó explained:
*"**Vibrating dust** refers to needling the **external channels** (#9), to dispel **yang disorders**; **lifting the veil** refers to needling the **convergence points** (*fǔshū*), to dispel **organ disorders**; **removing claws** refers to needling the **joints, limbs, and networks** (#10); **piercing garments** means exhaustively needling the **odd convergence points of all yang channels**; and **dispelling confusion** means fully understanding how to **harmonize yin and yang**, to **supplement what is deficient and drain what is excessive**, and to **adjust imbalances**."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When you speak of the stage *vibrating dust*, you say it involves needling the external channels to dispel yang disorders—but I do not understand what you mean. I wish to hear it fully."*

Qìbó replied:
*"When **vibrating dust** occurs, **yang qi is severely disordered**, surging upward and filling the chest. The patient **clenches their shoulders**, **breathes with restraint**, and **struggles for breath**, gasping and wheezing as if **repulsed by dust and smoke**. Their **diaphragm is locked**, and they **cannot exhale**—this is what is meant by *vibrating dust*. Even speaking of it now is **more urgent than the condition itself**."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. How should one treat it?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Treat it by needling **Tiānróng** [Celestial Container]."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"If coughing, upward breath, and chest pain persist, how should one treat it?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Needle **Liánquán** [Junction Spring]."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Are there fixed limits for these treatments?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"When needling **Tiānróng**, do not exceed one *cù* [~1.3 cm]. When needling **Liánquán**, bleed until the blood changes color before stopping."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When you speak of *opening the veil*, I do not grasp its meaning. What is *opening the veil*? The patient hears nothing, sees nothing—yet you say to needle the **palaces and conduits** to dispel **palace disorders**. Why is this so? I wish to hear the reason."*

Qìbó replied:
*"A profound question indeed! This is the essence of acupuncture, the pinnacle of needle technique, the realm of divine insight—words and texts cannot fully convey it. Let me speak of *opening the veil*, for even this is urgent beyond description."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. I wish to hear it fully."*

Qìbó replied:
*"To treat this, it must be done at **high noon**. Needle **Tīnggōng** [Palace of Hearing], striking the **pupil**. The sound will reach the ears—this is its conduit."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. What do you mean by *the sound reaching the ears*?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Needle the **pathogenic qi** while firmly pressing both nostrils with your hand, then swiftly lie down. The sound will surely respond to the needle."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. This is what is meant by *acting unseen yet unseen, without sight yet taking action*—where divine insight aligns."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When you speak of *removing claws*, you say to needle **joints and limb networks**—I wish to hear it fully."*

Qìbó replied:
*"The **lumbar and spine** are the body’s great joints; the **limb channels** are the pathways for movement. The **penis** is the body’s mechanism, the marker of **yin essence**, the conduit of **bodily fluids**. Thus, if diet is unregulated and emotions untimed, bodily fluids overflow inward, pooling in the **testicles**. When **blood pathways** are blocked, the **penis** remains erect without rest, bending and straightening becomes difficult, and movement is impaired. This condition resembles **water swelling**—neither ascending nor descending—visible like **metal and stone**, never concealed. Hence, it is called *removing claws*."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When you speak of *piercing garments*, you say to exhaustively needle all **yang’s extraordinary conduits**—yet there is no fixed location. I wish to hear it fully."*

Qìbó replied:
*"This is when **yang qi is excessive** while **yin qi is deficient**. If **yin is deficient**, internal heat arises; if **yang is excessive**, external heat follows. When internal heat converges, the chest burns like **embracing hot coals**. Externally, the patient fears **silk and cotton**, unable to bear nearness—neither to the body nor to bedding. When **pathways are obstructed**, sweat does not emerge. The tongue becomes **parched**, the lips **dry and cracked**, thirst unquenchable. They reject neither fine nor coarse foods."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. How should one treat it?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Needle **Tiānfǔ** [Celestial Warehouse], **Dàzhú** [Great Spine], and **Sānjié** [Three Deficiencies], and also needle **Zhōnglǒu** [Central Hollow] to dispel the heat. Supplement **Foot Hand Taiyin** [Spleen channel] to regulate sweat. When heat is gone and sweat is balanced, the condition resolves faster than *piercing garments*."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When you speak of *dispelling confusion*, you say to fully know how to **harmonize yin and yang**, to **supplement and drain excess and deficiency**, and to **shift imbalances**—how does this **dispel confusion**?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"When **great wind** afflicts the body, **blood and vessels** become uneven—**deficient** where lacking, **excessive** where full. Lightness and heaviness are unbalanced; the patient **lurches and tilts**, **stumbles without direction**, unaware of **west or east**, **north or south**, **ascending or descending**, **turning or overturning**—precisely **upside-down**, worse than mere confusion."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. How should one treat it?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Drain the excess, supplement the deficient, and restore **yin and yang** balance. Using the needle thus resolves confusion more swiftly."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"Excellent. I shall store this in the **Spiritual Orchid Chamber**, daring not to reveal it lightly."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"I have heard that acupuncture addresses **five perversions**—what are they?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"Diseases include those with **persistent rigidity**, **excessive swelling**, **constriction**, **heat**, and **cold**—these are the **five perversions**."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"How does one needle the **five perversions**?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"For all methods of needling the **five perversions**, there are no more than **five principles**:
- For **rigidity**, do not **meet the ridge** [of the spine]. Transform **common qi** to **adaptive nature**, avoid **pus formation**. If **fragile pathways** shift, remove the needle from its original site. If the patient is **unstable**, disperse the condition.
- For **excessive swelling**, gradually reduce size. Drain the excess, then supplement the deficient. **Sever the connection**, needle the **pathogenic qi**, and ensure **muscle adherence**. Observe for **no residue**, restore the **true qi**, and needle the **yang divisions of the flesh**.
- For **constriction**, gradually enlarge. Supplement the deficient to avoid harm. Observe its location and **meet the boundary**. If it cannot be **externally reached**, approach it **indirectly** until it **self-dissipates**, then needle the **flesh divisions**.
- For **heat**, **pierce and drain** until **blue-green** [indicating resolution], ensuring the **pathogenic qi escapes** without return. **Open pathways**, **unlock gates**, and allow the **evil to exit**—the disease will then cease.
- For **cold**, apply **warmth gradually**, moving **slowly** to **attune the spirit**. When **gates are closed**, **qi does not scatter**, and **deficiency and excess** are balanced, the **qi will stabilize**."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"How does one choose the needle?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"For **rigidity**, use a **metal needle**; for **excessive swelling**, a **sharp needle**; for **constriction**, a **round, sharp needle**; for **heat**, a **fine needle**; for **cold**, a **hair-thin needle**."*

*"Let me speak of **resolving theories**—harmonizing with **Heaven and Earth**, aligning with the **four seasons**, as humans **participate in Heaven and Earth**, thus able to resolve [disease]."*

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"When **gradual** (jiàn) **obstruction** (gā) occurs below and **reed-like** (wéi pú) **obstruction** arises above, this is how one discerns the **variation in form and *qi***."

*"**Yin and Yang** refer to **cold and heat**. When **heat** prevails, it engenders **rain** and manifests above, with **roots yellowing** and **juices diminishing**. Then, **human *qi* resides externally**, the **skin becomes slack**, the **defensive pathways** open, **blood and *qi* flow freely**, and **sweat pours out abundantly**, making the **skin moist and glistening**.

When **cold** prevails, the **earth congeals** and **water freezes**, while **human *qi* remains inward**, the **skin tightens**, the **defensive pathways close**, **sweat does not emerge**, **blood and *qi* grow strong**, and the **flesh becomes firm and dry**.

At such times, those skilled in **draining water** cannot proceed to **ice**; those adept at **piercing earth** cannot **break through frozen ground**. Even those proficient in **needling** cannot **extract the four *jùés*** (obstructions). If **blood vessels congeal** and **solidify**, preventing **free circulation**, they cannot yet be treated as **softened**.

Thus, **draining water** requires waiting until **Heaven’s warmth thaws the ice**, the **frost dissolves**, and **water can flow**; only then can **earth be pierced**. **Human vessels** are the same—when treating **obstruction**, one must first **warm and harmonize the channels**, adjusting **palms to armpits**, **elbows to knees**, and **neck to spine**. Once **fire *qi* circulates**, the **blood vessels flow**, and then one may **examine the disease**. If the **pulse is slack and glistening**, needle and **level it**; if **tight and firm**, **pierce and disperse it**. When the **obstructed *qi* descends**, the condition ceases—this is called **resolving congealed *qi***.

The **categories of needling** lie in **balancing *qi***—when *qi* **congests in the stomach**, it is **dispersed to harmonize the defensive and nutritive pathways**, each **following its proper course**. **Prenatal *qi*** (zōngqì) **lingers in the Sea of *Qi*** (Hǎi), its **lower aspect** **converges at the *Qi* Street** (Qìjiē), and its **upper aspect** **ascends through the Breathing Pathway** (Xìdào). Thus, if **obstruction occurs in the feet**, **prenatal *qi* does not descend**, and the **blood within the pulse congeals**, **stagnating**—unless **warmed with fire**, it cannot be **drawn out**. The **needler must first observe** the **fullness or emptiness** of the **channels and collaterals**, **probing and tracing them**, **pressing and percussing**, and **needling where the *qi* responds** before **extracting and descending it**.

When the **Six Channels** are **balanced**, it is called **no disease**; even if **diseased**, it is called **self-correction**. If **one channel** is **upperly full and lowerly empty**, **blocked**, it must have **crossing collaterals** **excessively pressing upon the main channel**, **obstructing its flow**. **Observe and disperse them**—this is called **resolving congealed *qi***.

For **upper cold and lower heat**, first needle the **Neck’s Greater Yang** (Tǎiyáng), **retaining the needle for a long time**. After needling, **warm the neck and shoulders**, allowing the **heat to descend** and **merge** until the condition ceases—this is called **pushing upward**.

For **upper heat and lower cold**, **observe the empty pulse** and **insert it into the channels and collaterals** to **extract the obstruction**; when the *qi* **descends**, the condition ceases—this is called **drawing downward**.

For **severe heat throughout the body**, where one **rages and sees, hears, and speaks delusions** (wànjiàn, wànwén, wàngyán), needle the **Foot’s Greater Yang Brightness** (Yángmíng) **channel and its major collaterals**. **Supplement the empty**, and **dispersion the full**—**blood**—and then, **with the patient reclining**, **stand at the head**, using **both hands’ four fingers** to **clasp and press the carotid pulse**, holding firmly. **Roll and push downward**, reaching the **mid-sternum** (Quēpén), then **return as before**. When the **heat departs**, the condition ceases—this is called **pushing and dispersing**.

The Yellow Emperor said:
*"There is a pulse that generates **dozens of diseases**—some **painful**, some **obstructed**, some **hot**, some **cold**, some **itchy**, some **numb**, some **unresponsive**—endless **transformations**. What is its cause?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"These all arise from **evil *qi***. The Yellow Emperor said: *"I have heard that *qi* has **True *Qi*** (Zhēnqì), **Proper *Qi*** (Zhèngqì), and **Evil *Qi*** (Xiéqì). What is **True *Qi***?"*

Qìbó replied:
*"**True *Qi*** is what one **receives from Heaven**, **conjoined with grain *qi*** (gǔqì) to **fill the body**. **Proper *Qi*** is **correcting wind** (Zhèngfēng), **coming from one direction**, neither **excessive wind** nor **deficient wind**. **Evil *Qi*** is the **harmful wind** (Xūfēng) that **assaults and injures** people. When it **penetrates deeply**, it **cannot depart on its own**. **Correcting wind**, however, **penetrates shallowly**, **merging and departing naturally**. Its **gentle and weak** nature **cannot overcome True *Qi***, so it **departs of its own accord**."*

*"When **deficient evil** penetrates the body, it **stirs the form** with **alcohol-like agitation** (jiǔzhì), **raises the body hair**, and **opens the defensive pathways**. If it **enters deeply**, it **internally assails the bones**, causing **bone numbness** (gǔbì). If it **assails the sinews**, it causes **sinew spasm** (jīnluán). If it **confronts the pulse**, it **blocks the blood**, **resulting in obstruction**. If it **assails the flesh**, it **clashes with defensive *qi***—when **Yang prevails**, it causes **heat**; when **Yin prevails**, it causes **cold**. **Cold** drives **True *Qi* away**; **True *Qi* departs**, leaving **emptiness**; **emptiness** **engenders cold**.*

If it **confronts between the skin and flesh**, its **evil *qi* manifests externally**, **opening the defensive pathways**, **spreading the body hair**, and **allowing *qi* to circulate freely**—this causes **itching** (yǎng). If it **lingers without departing**, it causes **numbness** (bì). When **defensive *qi* does not circulate**, it **shuts down** like **a shot horse**, causing **unresponsiveness** (bùrén).

When **deficient evil** **concentrates in the body’s half**, and **penetrates deeply**, it **resides internally in the nutritive and defensive pathways**. As the **nutritive and defensive pathways gradually decline**, **True *Qi* departs**, and **evil *qi* remains alone**, **manifesting as hemiplegia** (piāngǔ).

If the **evil *qi* is shallow**, it causes **pulse pain on one side** (piāntòng).

When **deficient evil** **deeply enters the body**, **cold and heat clash**, **lingering internally**—if **cold overcomes heat**, it causes **bone pain and flesh withering** (ròujī). If **heat overcomes cold**, it **rots the flesh**, **corrupts the muscles**, and **forms pus**; internally, it **injures the bones**, **leading to bone necrosis** (gǔshí).

If **a sinew suddenly contracts**, the **sinew bends and cannot extend**, and **evil *qi* lodges between them**, **unable to reverse**, it **manifests as sinew obstruction** (jīnliú).

If **a mass forms**, **with *qi* converging** and **defensive *qi* lingering**, it **cannot reverse**, and **fluids stagnate over time**, **merging to form intestinal masses** (chángliú)—if **lingering for years**, they **become firm** under hand pressure.

If **a mass forms** and **fluids stagnate**, **evil *qi* invades it**, **congealing and worsening daily**, **clustering together**, it **becomes a cancerous tumor** (yīnliú)—**firm under hand pressure**.

If **a mass forms** and **deeply invades the bone**, **with *qi* adhering to the bone**, the **bone and *qi* grow ever larger**, it **becomes bone cancer** (gǔjù).

If **a mass forms** and **invades the flesh**, **with prenatal *qi* converging**, and **evil *qi* lingering without departing**, it **forms pus if there is heat**, or **flesh cancer** (ròujù) **if there is none**.

「In general, these several *qi* movements have no fixed locations where they manifest, yet they bear constant names.

*(Huangdi Neijing Lingshu Jizhu, Volume 21, *Zhī Guānnèng* [Knowing the Functions of the Organs] as "Zhī" [Support]; Crimes as "Bǎ" [Hold], harmonizing with the later explanation in this chapter; Yang as originally "Wǔ" [Five], corrected according to *Taishang* [Supreme Authenticity] Volume 19, *Zhī Guānnèng*; Trembling as "Yáo" [Shake]; Great as "Chí" [Hold], according to *Taishang* Volume 15, *Chǐ Zhěn* [Inch Diagnosis]; Coarse as "Lián" [Sharp], as in *Jia-Yi Jing* [The Canon of A and B] Volume 4, Section 2. Left as originally "Right," corrected according to *Jia-Yi Jing* Volume 12, Section 6; Split as originally "Biàn" [Distinguish], corrected from the *Zhāofù Jùjìng Táng* [Respectful Study Hall of Zhao] edition. *Qi* as originally omitted, corrected from the *Zhāofù Jùjìng Táng* edition; Split as "Zhī" [Support] in *Taishang* Volume 22, *Wǔ Jié Cì* [Five Node Punctures], same below. Dust as originally "Zhèn" [Shake], corrected from the *Zhāofù Jùjìng Táng* edition; Hook as "Xún" [Ask]; Ask as originally "Wén" [Listen], corrected from the *Zhāofù Jùjìng Táng* edition. Good as "Yīyī Rèn" [One by One Recognize] in *Taishang* Volume 22, *Wǔ Cì Jié*; Blood as originally "Shuǐ" [Water]; Brittle as "Guǐ" [Deceptive]; Cyan as "Cāng" [Deep Blue]; Skin as originally "Ròu" [Flesh]. *Bianróng* [Discerning Appearance] as "Piānkè" [Partial Guest] in *Lingshu Lüè Liùqì Lùnpiān* [Abridged Chapter on the Six *Qi* Movements].

*(Note: "Líu" [Drifting Mass] as "Liú" [Tumor] in *Jia-Yi Jing* Volume 11, Section 9; same for "Chángliú" [Intestinal Drifting Mass]. "Jù" [Cancerous] here likely ought to be "Liú" [Tumor], same for "Ròujù" [Flesh Tumor] below.)

*(Huangdi Neijing Lingshu Jizhu, Volume 22, *Weìqì Xíng* [The Movement of Defensive *Qi*], Chapter 76.)」

The Yellow Emperor asked Qìbó#1, saying: *"I wish to hear of the movement of Defensive *Qi* and its ebb and flow in conjunction with the day and night—how does it proceed?"*

Qíbó Gāo replied: *"The year has twelve months, the day has twelve *chén* [time divisions], with *Zǐ* [Midnight] and *Wǔ* [Noon] as the *jīng* [vertical meridians], and *Mǎo* [5 AM] and *Yǒu* [5 PM] as the *wěi* [horizontal meridians]. The heavens encompass twenty-eight *xiù* [constellations], and each constellation has seven stars, making four times seven—twenty-eight stars in total—with *Fáng* [Room] and *Xiè* [Arrow] as the horizontal meridians, and *Xū* [Empty] and *Zhāng* [Full] as the vertical meridians.

Thus, from *Fáng* to *Bì* [Gradation] is *yáng* [Yang], and from *Áng* [Upright] to *Wěi* [Tail] is *yīn* [Yin]. *Yáng* governs the day, *yīn* governs the night. Therefore, the Defensive *Qi* circulates fifty times through the body in one day and night, twenty-five times in the *yáng* channels during the day, and twenty-five times in the *yīn* channels at night, completing a full cycle through the five *zàng* [viscera]#2.

Hence, on a balanced day, when *yīn* is fully exhausted, *yáng qi* emerges from the eyes. When the eyes open, the *qi* ascends to the head, then follows the *Tàiyáng* [Greater Yang] pathway down the nape to the tips of the toes. Its dispersed branches diverge from the eyes at the *Ruìbì* [Sharp Division], descend along the hand’s *Tàiyáng* channel, and reach the outer lateral side of the little finger’s joint. Its dispersed branches also diverge from the eyes at the *Ruìbì*, descend along the foot’s *Shàoyáng* [Lesser Yang] channel, and enter the joint between the little and second toes. Above, it follows the *Shàoyáng* [Lesser Yang] division of the hand, descending to the joint of the little finger#3. The diverging branches ascend to the ear’s front, converge with the *Kēmài* [Jaw Pulse], descend along the foot’s *Yángmíng* [Yang Brilliance], and proceed downward to the *Dù* [Knee] joint, entering the spaces between the five toes.

When dispersed, it descends from beneath the ear along the hand’s *Yángmíng* channel, entering the joint of the thumb, and reaching the center of the palm. When it reaches the foot, it enters the sole, emerges beneath the inner ankle, travels along the *yīn* divisions, and returns to converge with the eyes, thus completing one cycle.

Therefore, when the Defensive *Qi* travels one *shě* [segment], the human *qi* circulates one full cycle through the body plus eight-tenths of a segment#4; when it travels two *shě*, the human *qi* circulates three full cycles plus six-tenths of a segment#5; when it travels three *shě*, the human *qi* circulates five full cycles plus four-tenths of a segment; when it travels four *shě*, the human *qi* circulates seven full cycles plus two-tenths of a segment; when it travels five *shě*, the human *qi* circulates nine full cycles; when it travels six *shě*, the human *qi* circulates ten full cycles plus eight-tenths of a segment; when it travels seven *shě*, the human *qi* circulates twelve full cycles plus six-tenths of a segment; when it travels fourteen *shě*, the human *qi* completes twenty-five full cycles plus two-tenths of a segment, marking the exhaustion of *yáng* and the commencement of *yīn*, which then receives the *qi*.

When the Defensive *Qi* first enters the *yīn* divisions, it consistently ascends from the foot’s *Shàoyǐn* [Lesser Yin] channel to the kidney, then to the heart, the heart to the lungs, the lungs to the liver, the liver to the spleen, and finally the spleen returns to the kidney, completing one cycle.

Thus, when the Defensive *Qi* travels one *shě* at night, the human *qi* circulates once through the *yīn zàng* [viscera] plus eight-tenths of a segment, equivalent to twenty-five cycles of *yáng* circulation, and then converges again with the eyes. In one day and night, the combined circulation of *yáng* and *yīn* Defensive *Qi* is twenty-five full cycles plus two-tenths of a segment#6, and ten full cycles through the viscera#7. Hence, the reason why some people awaken earlier or later is due to the incomplete exhaustion of the *qi*’s odd fractions.

The Yellow Emperor said: *"The Defensive *Qi* within the body moves upward and downward without fixed intervals. How should one observe the *qi* and apply acupuncture accordingly?"*

Qíbó Gāo replied: *"The divisions vary in extent, and the days differ in length. Spring, autumn, winter, and summer each have their own proportions and principles. Therefore, one must always take *píngdàn* [Dawn] as the starting point and the end of night as the beginning.

Thus, one day and night comprises a hundred *kè* [moments], with twenty-five *kè* marking half a day’s measure. It is always thus without variation, ceasing when the sun sets and following the day’s length and shortness as reference points for observation and treatment.

If one carefully observes the timing, the disease can be accurately predicted; if one misses the timing and observes in reverse, no disease can be cured. Hence it is said: ‘To treat *shí* [repletion], one must puncture at its arrival; to treat *xū* [depletion], one must puncture at its departure.’ This refers to the moments of the *qi*’s presence or absence, observing depletion and repletion to determine the acupuncture treatment.

Therefore, one must carefully observe where the Defensive *Qi* resides and puncture accordingly—this is called *féngshí* [Meeting the Timing]. If a disease lies in the three *yáng* channels, one must observe when the Defensive *Qi* is in the *yáng* divisions before puncturing; if a disease lies in the three *yīn* channels, one must observe when the Defensive *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions before puncturing.

When the Defensive *Qi* has descended one *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel; when it has descended two *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Shàoyáng* channel; when it has descended three *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Yángmíng* channel; when it has descended four *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions. When it has descended five *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel; when it has descended six *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Shàoyáng* channel; when it has descended seven *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Yángmíng* channel; when it has descended eight *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions. When it has descended nine *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel; when it has descended ten *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Shàoyáng* channel; when it has descended eleven *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Yángmíng* channel; when it has descended twelve *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions. When it has descended thirteen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel; when it has descended fourteen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Shàoyáng* channel; when it has descended fifteen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Yángmíng* channel; when it has descended sixteen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions. When it has descended seventeen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel; when it has descended eighteen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Shàoyáng* channel; when it has descended nineteen *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Yángmíng* channel; when it has descended twenty *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions. When it has descended twenty-one *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel; when it has descended twenty-two *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Shàoyáng* channel; when it has descended twenty-three *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Yángmíng* channel; when it has descended twenty-four *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *yīn* divisions. When it has descended twenty-five *kè*, the human *Qi* is in the *Tàiyáng* channel—this marks half a day’s measure.

From *Fáng* to *Bì* is fourteen *shě*, descending fifty *kè* and completing half a day’s cycle; it then reverses its course, traveling one *shě*, descending three *kè* and four-sevenths of a *kè*."*

The essential principle states: When the sun’s *kè* accumulate upon the previous *xiù* (宿), the human *Qi* resides in the *Tàiyáng* channel. Therefore, as the sun travels one *shě* (舍), the human *Qi* flows through three *Yáng* channels and the *Yīn* divisions—ever thus without end. Heaven and Earth follow the same reckoning, their movements ceaseless and cyclical, completing a full day and night in a hundred *kè* before returning to their beginning.

---
**Phonetic Annotation:**
*Pàn* (盼) is pronounced *Pǔbàbiē* (盼普巴切).

---
**The Eight Winds of the Nine Palaces (Chapter Seventy-Seventh):**
The *Tàiyī* (太一) abides in the *Xūdiàn* (吁垫) Palace for forty-six days at the Winter Solstice; the next day, it resides in the *Tiānlíu* (天留) Palace for forty-six days; the following day, it resides in the *Cāngmén* (仓门) Palace for forty-six days; the next day, it resides in the *Yīnluò* (阴洛) Palace for forty-five days; the following day, it resides in the *Shàngtiān* (上天) Palace for forty-six days; the next day, it resides in the *Xuánwěi* (玄委) Palace for forty-six days; the following day, it resides in the *Cāngguǒ* (仓果) Palace for forty-six days; the next day, it resides in the *Xīnluò* (新洛) Palace for forty-five days; thereafter, it returns to the *Xūdiàn* Palace, marking the completion of the Winter Solstice cycle.

The *Tàiyī* traverses the Palaces daily: beginning at the Winter Solstice in the *Xūdiàn* Palace, it counts the days in sequence from one to nine, then reverses its course back to one, ever thus without end, completing its cycle.

When the *Tàiyī* shifts its abode, Heaven responds with wind and rain. If wind and rain occur on that day, it is auspicious, and the year will bring prosperity, contentment, and few illnesses. If the wind and rain precede its movement, there will be excessive rain; if they follow, there will be drought.

If the *Tàiyī* exhibits variation on the Winter Solstice, it portends changes in the ruler;
If it exhibits variation on the Spring Equinox, it portends changes in the minister;
If it exhibits variation on the Mid-Palace day, it portends changes in the officials;
If it exhibits variation on the Autumn Equinox, it portends changes in the generals;
If it exhibits variation on the Summer Solstice, it portends changes among the common people.

By "exhibits variation," it is meant that when the *Tàiyī* resides in the five Palaces, the winds cause disease: the *Dàruò* (大弱) Wind uproots trees, stirs sand and stones, each according to its governing influence, determining noble or ignoble outcomes based on the direction from which the wind arises.

If the wind comes from the Palace where the *Tàiyī* resides, it is called a *shí* (实) Wind, nurturing life and fostering all things;
If it comes from the Palace opposite its abode, it is called a *xū* (虚) Wind, harming people, bringing death and calamity.

Thus, the Sage avoids *xū* (虚) Winds, shunning the *xié* (邪) path daily like one evading arrows and stones. Evil winds cannot then harm, and this is the reason.

Therefore, when the *Tàiyī* enters and establishes itself in the central Palace, it surveys the eight winds to divine auspiciousness or inauspiciousness.

The wind from the south is called the *Dàruò* (大弱) Wind; its harm to humans lodges internally in the Heart, externally in the Pulse, and its *Qi* governs heat.
The wind from the southwest is called the *Móu* (谋) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Spleen, externally in the muscles, and its *Qi* governs weakness.
The wind from the west is called the *Gāng* (刚) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Lungs, externally in the skin, and its *Qi* governs dryness.
The wind from the northwest is called the *Zhé* (折) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Small Intestine, externally in the *Tàiyáng* Pulse of the hand. If the pulse is severed, it overflows; if the pulse is closed, it stagnates and fails to flow, often resulting in sudden death.
The wind from the north is called the *Dàgāng* (大刚) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Kidneys, externally in the bones and the sinews of the shoulders and back, and its *Qi* governs cold.
The wind from the northeast is called the *Xiōng* (凶) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Large Intestine, externally in the ribs, armpits, clavicles, and limbs.
The wind from the east is called the *Yīngér* (婴儿) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Liver, externally in the sinews and tendons, and its *Qi* governs dampness of the body.
The wind from the southeast is called the *Ruò* (弱) Wind; its harm lodges internally in the Stomach, externally in the muscles, and its *Qi* governs heaviness of the body.

These eight winds, when arising from their respective *xū* (虚) Palaces, can cause illness in humans. When three *xū* (虚) winds converge, they bring sudden violent illness and death.
When two *shí* (实) winds and one *xū* (虚) wind clash, illness manifests as *línlù* (淋露) with alternating cold and heat.
If one violates the wind’s damp and wet domains, it results in *wěi* (痿) paralysis.

Thus, the Sage avoids the winds as one avoids arrows and stones.

If one encounters three *xū* (虚) winds and is struck by an *xié* (邪) wind, it leads to sudden collapse and partial withering.

---
**The Nine Needles (Chapter Seventy-Eighth):**
The Yellow Emperor said: "I have heard of the Nine Needles from the Master, and they are vast and profound. Yet I still do not fully comprehend them. May I ask their origin and why they bear this name?"

Qībó (岐伯) replied: "The Nine Needles are the grand numbers of Heaven and Earth, beginning with one and ending with nine. Thus, it is said:
One follows the Dao of Heaven,
Two follows the Dao of Earth,
Three follows the Dao of humanity,
Four follows the Dao of the seasons,
Five follows the Dao of sound,
Six follows the Dao of law,
Seven follows the Dao of stars,
Eight follows the Dao of winds,
Nine follows the Dao of the wilds."

The Yellow Emperor said: "How does one apply the needles in response to these nine numbers?"

Qībó replied: "The Sage, in establishing the numbers of Heaven and Earth, took one and multiplied it by nine, thus creating the nine wilds. Nine times nine is eighty-one, which gave rise to the *Huángzhōng* (黄锺) reckoning. The needles are applied in accordance with these numbers.

One represents Heaven. Heaven is the *Yáng* (阳)."

The five *zàng* (内藏/viscera) that correspond to Heaven are the lungs. The lungs are the covering of the five *zàng* and six *fǔ* (外府/entrails), and the skin is their paired counterpart, the *yáng* (阳) of humanity. Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its head large and its tip sharp, ensuring it does not penetrate deeply and allowing *yáng* qi to emerge.

Two represents Earth. The means by which humanity corresponds to soil is through the flesh. Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its body hollow and its tip round, ensuring it does not harm the flesh. If it does, the qi will be exhausted.

Three represents humanity. The means by which humanity achieves life is through the blood and vessels. Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its body broad and its tip round, allowing it to press upon the vessels without sinking in, so as to direct its qi and let the evil qi exit alone.

Four represents the seasons. The seasons and the eight winds are guests within the meridians and collaterals, causing painful *bìng* (病/illness). Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its body hollow and its tip sharp, allowing it to disperse heat and draw out blood, thus exhausting the ailment.

Five represents sound. Sound divides winter and summer, distinguishing *yīn* (阴) and *yáng* (阳) at the *zǐ* (子) and *wǔ* (午) points. When cold and heat contend, the two qi clash, combining to form *tān* (痰/phlegm) and *nóng* (脓/pus). Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its tip like a sword’s edge, allowing it to extract large pus.

Six represents law. Law harmonizes *yīn* and *yáng*, the four seasons, and the twelve primary meridians. When empty evils lodge in the meridians, they cause sudden *bì* (痹/numbness or stagnation). Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its point like a *wù* (骛/falcon’s talon), both round and sharp, with a slightly enlarged middle, to extract sudden evil qi.

Seven represents stars. Stars correspond to the seven orifices of humanity. When evils lodge in the meridians and cause painful *bì* (痹), they reside in the collaterals. Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its point like the proboscis of a mosquito or gnat, inserting gently and slowly, lingering briefly, allowing the correct qi to follow, so that both true and false evils depart, and the needle is withdrawn to nourish.

Eight represents wind. Wind corresponds to the eight major joints of the limbs—*gǔ* (股/thigh), *jīng* (肱/upper arm), and the eight nodes. The empty winds of the eight directions harm humanity, lodging internally between bones, joints, waist, spine, and the pathways of the sinews, causing deep *bì* (痹). Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its body long and its tip sharp, allowing it to probe and extract distant and deep evils.

Nine represents the wilds. The wilds correspond to the joints, sinews, and skin of humanity. When licentious evils overflow the body, like the state of wind and water, they cannot pass beyond the major joints and nodes. Therefore, when treating with needles, one must make its point like a *tǐng* (挺/straight staff), with a slightly rounded edge, to extract the great qi that cannot pass the joints.

The Yellow Emperor said: "Are there fixed lengths for the needles?"

Qībó replied: "The first is the *jìng* needle (镜针), modeled after the *jīn* needle (巾针), with its tip shortened by half an inch, sharpened to a length of one inch and six *fēn* (分/0.1 inch), used for treating heat in the head and body. The second is the *yuán* needle (员针), modeled after the *xù* needle (絮针), with its body hollowed and its tip sharpened, one inch and six *fēn* long, used for treating qi lodged between layers. The third is the *tí* needle (缇针), modeled after the sharpness of millet and sorghum grains, three inches and five *fēn* long, used for pressing upon vessels and extracting qi, allowing evil to depart. The fourth is the *fēng* needle (锋针), modeled after the *xù* needle (絮针), with its body hollowed and its tip sharp, one inch and six *fēn* long, used for treating *tān* (痰/phlegm) and heat, drawing out blood. The fifth is the *bì* needle (铍针), modeled after a sword’s edge, two *fēn* and five *lì* (分/0.1 inch, 厘/0.01 inch) wide, four inches long, used for extracting large phlegm and pus, treating cases where cold and heat contend. The sixth is the *yuán lì* needle (圆利针), modeled after the *áo* needle (鳌针), with its tip slightly enlarged and its body narrowed, allowing it to probe internally, one inch and six *fēn* long, used for extracting *bì* (痹/numbness or stagnation). The seventh is the *háo* needle (毫针), modeled after fine hairs, one inch and six *fēn* long, used for treating cold, heat, pain, and *bì* (痹) in the collaterals. The eighth is the *cháng* needle (长针), modeled after the *cài* needle (蔡针), seven inches long, used for extracting deep and distant evils. The ninth is the *dà* needle (大针), modeled after the *fēng* needle (锋针), with its tip slightly rounded, four inches long, used for extracting great qi that cannot pass the joints. Thus, the nine needles’ shapes—large, small, long, and short—are complete.

The Yellow Emperor said: "I wish to hear how the body corresponds to the nine wilds."

Qībó replied: "Let me explain how the body corresponds to the nine wilds. The left foot corresponds to *Lìchūn* (立春/Spring Begins), on the days of *wùyín-jǐchǒu* (戊寅/戊子, 己丑/己亥); the left side (胁) corresponds to *Chūnfēn* (春分/Spring Equinox), on the days of *yǐmǎo* (乙卯); the left hand corresponds to *Lìxià* (立夏/Summer Begins), on the days of *wùchén-jǐsì* (戊辰/戊子, 己巳/己亥); the chest, throat, and head correspond to *Xiàzhì* (夏至/Summer Solstice), on the days of *bǐngwǔ* (丙午); the right hand corresponds to *Lìqiū* (立秋/Autumn Begins), on the days of *wùshēn-jǐwèi* (戊申/戊子, 己未/己亥); the right side (胁) corresponds to *Qiūfēn* (秋分/Autumn Equinox), on the days of *xīnyǒu* (辛酉); the right foot corresponds to *Lìdōng* (立冬/Winter Begins), on the days of *wùxū-jǐhài* (戊戌/戊子, 己亥/己亥); the waist, lower abdomen, and lower orifices correspond to *Dōngzhì* (冬至/Winter Solstice), on the days of *rénzǐ* (壬子). The six *fǔ* (外府/entrails) and the diaphragm below the three *zàng* (内藏/viscera) correspond to the central regions, with their great prohibitions. The great prohibitions are on the days when *Tàiyī* (太一/the Grand Unity) resides and on all *wù-jǐ* (戊己) days. These nine correspondences must be carefully observed to determine where the eight winds lodge. If there are *tān* (痰/phlegm) or *zhǒng* (肿/swelling) in the upper, lower, left, or right regions of the body, one must not treat directly on the day it manifests, for that is the *tiān jì rì* (天忌日/heavenly forbidden day).

When the form is joyful and the will is sorrowful, illness arises in the vessels, and it is treated with *jiǔ* (灸/moxibustion) and *cì* (刺/needling). When the form is sorrowful and the will is joyful, illness arises in the sinews, and it is treated with *wū* (熨/ironing) and *yǐn* (引/pulling). When the form is joyful and the will is joyful, illness arises in the flesh, and it is treated with needles and stones. When the form is sorrowful and the will is sorrowful, illness arises in the throat and voice, and it is treated with sweet medicines. When the form is frequently startled and terrified, the sinews and vessels are obstructed, illness arises in the lack of sensation, and it is treated with *ànmó* (按摩/massage) and *niàngyào* (酿药/fermented medicines). This is called the *xíng* (形/physical form).

The five *zàng* (内藏/viscera) qi: the heart governs *yì* (噫/sighing), the lungs govern *ké* (咳/coughing), the liver governs *yǔ* (语/speaking), the spleen governs *tūn* (吞/swallowing), and the kidneys govern *qiàn* (欠/yawning).
The six *fǔ* (外府/entrails) qi: the gallbladder governs *nù* (怒/anger), the stomach governs *qìniào* (气逆/reverse peristalsis) and *huì* (秽/foulness), the large and small intestines govern *xiè* (泄/diarrhea), the bladder’s failure to restrain governs *yíniào* (遗溺/incontinence), and the lower *jiāo* (焦/lower burner) overflow governs *shuǐ* (水/water-related disorders).

The Five Flavors:
Sour enters the liver, pungent enters the lungs, bitter enters the heart, sweet enters the spleen, salty enters the kidneys, bland enters the stomach. This is called the Five Flavors.

The Five Convergences:
When *jīng* (精/essence) qi converges upon the liver, there is melancholy;
when upon the heart, there is joy;
when upon the lungs, there is sorrow;
when upon the kidneys, there is fear;
when upon the spleen, there is apprehension.
This is called the convergence of the Five Essences upon the viscera.

The Five Detestations:
The liver detests wind,
the heart detests heat,
the lungs detest cold,
the kidneys detest dryness,
the spleen detests dampness.
These are the detestations of the Five Viscera.

The Five Fluids:
The heart governs sweat,
the liver governs tears,
the lungs govern nasal mucus,
the kidneys govern saliva,
the spleen governs saliva (oral fluid).
These are the origins of the Five Fluids.

The Five Exhaustions:
Prolonged vision injures blood,
prolonged exposure injures qi,
prolonged sitting injures flesh,
prolonged standing injures bones,
prolonged walking injures sinews.
These are the illnesses of the Five Prolonged Exertions.

The Five Movements:
Sour moves through the sinews,
pungent moves through the qi,
bitter moves through the blood,
salty moves through the bones,
sweet moves through the flesh.
This is called the Five Movements.

The Five Restraints:
If illness is in the sinews, avoid sour foods;
if in the qi, avoid pungent foods;
if in the bones, avoid salty foods;
if in the blood, avoid bitter foods;
if in the flesh, avoid sweet foods.
Though the mouth may crave them, do not consume them in excess—restrain yourself. This is called the Five Restraints.

The Five Manifestations:
Yin illnesses manifest in the bones,
yang illnesses manifest in the blood,
flavors manifest in the qi.
Yang illnesses manifest in winter,
yin illnesses manifest in summer.

The Five Pathologies:
When evil enters the yang, it becomes mania;
when evil enters the yin, it becomes blood stasis.
When evil enters the yang and turns, it becomes epilepsy;
when evil enters the yin and turns, it becomes sores.
When yin enters the yang, the illness is tranquil;
when yin exits to the yang, the illness is prone to anger.

The Five Viscera:
The heart houses *shén* (神/spirit),
the lungs house *pò* (魄/ethereal soul),
the liver houses *hún* (魂/ethereal soul),
the spleen houses *yì* (意/intent),
the kidneys house *jīngzhì* (精志/essence-will).

The Five Governances:
The heart governs the vessels,
the lungs govern the skin,
the liver governs the sinews,
the spleen governs the muscles,
the kidneys govern the bones.

The Six Yang-Yin:
*Yángmíng* (阳明) has abundant blood and abundant qi,
*Tàiyáng* (太阳) has abundant blood and scarce qi,
*Shàoyáng* (少阳) has abundant qi and scarce blood,
*Tàiyīn* (太阴) has abundant blood and scarce qi,
*Juéyīn* (厥阴) has abundant blood and scarce qi,
*Shàoyīn* (少阴) has abundant qi and scarce blood.
Thus it is said:
To puncture *Yángmíng* releases blood and qi,
to puncture *Tàiyáng* releases blood and evil qi,
to puncture *Shàoyáng* releases qi and evil blood,
to puncture *Tàiyīn* releases blood and evil qi,
to puncture *Juéyīn* releases blood and evil qi,
to puncture *Shàoyīn* releases qi and evil blood.

The Foot Yin-Yang Pairings:
*Yángmíng* and *Tàiyīn* are exterior-interior,
*Shàoyáng* and *Juéyīn* are exterior-interior,
*Tàiyáng* and *Shàoyīn* are exterior-interior.
This is called the yin-yang of the foot.

The Hand Yin-Yang Pairings:
*Yángmíng* and *Tàiyīn* are exterior-interior,
*Shàoyáng* and the *Xīnzhǔ* (心主/Heart Governor) are exterior-interior,
*Tàiyáng* and *Shàoyīn* are exterior-interior.
This is called the yin-yang of the hand.

**[Phonetic Note]**
*Tóng* (筒) is pronounced the same as *tóng* (同).

「Tí is pronounced *dī*.
*Jīnzhēn* (pericardium needle) is alternatively written as *Bùzhēn* (cloth needle).
*Wǔzǒu* is pronounced *gēng*.
*Wǔcái* is written as *Wǔjìn* in the *Su Wèn* (Plain Questions).

**From *Língshū* (Spiritual Pivot) *Jíjiǔ* (Collection of Annotations) Volume 22:**

#1 Qíbó (岐伯) is written as *Bógāo* (伯高) in *Tàisū* (Great Essentials) Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu* (Fifty Circuits of Defense).

#2 *Zàng* (藏) was originally written as *suì* (岁), corrected according to *Tàisū* Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu*.

#3 *Xiǎozhǐ* (小指) has the additional phrase *cìzhǐ* (次指, "sequential finger") in *Tàisū* Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu*.

#4 *Qìxíng* (气行) has the additional phrase *yú shēn* (於身, "in the body") in *Jiǎyǔ Jīng* (Classics of the *Jiǎ* and *Yǔ*) Volume 1, 9th line.

#5 *Sān* (三) was originally written as *èr* (二), corrected according to *Tàisū* Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu*.

#6 *Èr* (二) was originally written as *sì* (四), corrected according to *Tàisū* Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu*.

#7 *Èr* (二) was originally written as *sì* (四), corrected according to *Tàisū* Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu*.

#8 *Bùyǐ qī* (不以期) is written as *Wú jǐqí* (无己其) in *Jiǎyǔ Jīng* Volume 1, 9th line. The character *qí* (其) belongs to the following phrase.

#9 *Bìng* (病) was originally omitted, supplemented according to *Tàisū* Volume 12, *Wèi Wǔshízhōu*.

#10 *Yī* (一) was originally written as *èr* (二), corrected according to the *Zhào Fǔ Jùjìngtáng* (Zhao Residence Rectitude Hall) edition.

#11 *Rìxíng bàn dù* (日行半度) is written as *Xián rì zhī dù yě* (闲日之度也) in *Jiǎyǔ Jīng* Volume 1, 9th line. The following also includes the phrase: *"From *Cóng'áng* (昂) to *Xīn* (心), also fourteen *hé* (合), water descends fifty *kè* (刻), the daily degree also."*

#12 *Shàngtiān* (上天) was originally written as *Tiānguān* (天官), corrected according to *Tàisū* Volume 28, *Jiǔgōng Bāfēng* (Nine Palaces, Eight Winds).

#13 *Hàn* (旱) was originally written as *hàn* (汗), corrected according to *Tàisū* Volume 28, *Jiǔgōng Bāfēng*.

#14 *Zài* (在) was originally written as *yǒu* (有), corrected according to the *Zhào Fǔ Jùjìngtáng* edition.»

#15 **Syndrome** (症): Originally written as **"lump" (瘤)**, corrected according to *Jiǎyǔ Jīng* Volume 5, 2nd line.
#16 **Its** (其): The *Zhào Fǔ Jùjìngtáng* edition reads **"thus" (故)**.
#17 **Sharp** (尖): Originally written as the two characters **"small large" (小大)**, corrected according to the *Zhào Fǐ Jùjìngtáng* edition.
#18 **Hand** (手): Originally written as **"hair" (毛)**, corrected according to the *Zhào Fǔ Jùjìngtáng* edition.
#19 **Form** (形): In *Jiǎyǔ Jīng* Volume 6, 2nd line, it reads **"Five Forms Doctrine" (五形志也)**.
#20 **Excess** (多): The *Zhào Fǔ Jùjìngtáng* edition reads **"deficiency" (少)**.
